  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_ad5a0106-8345-4fcf-938d-a70f66ce41fc'
      });
    }

      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

  <span id="freeText14476758619321636100" style="display:none">Have you found that your life is stuck in a rut? Do you want to experience more joy, passion and play in your everyday life?<br />You can, with the help of this book!<br /><br />For millions of people the world over, life can be an unending repetition of drudgery that shows no sign of ever ceasing. It can happen anywhere and to anyone, if you are caught in a cycle where you simply exist, react to life and never really ‘feel’ life’s amazing vibrancy.<br /><br />In this book, Dancing with The Field: Bringing Joy, Passion and Play into Everyday Life, a new concept is explored around the conscious field that responds to us as we interact with it, with chapters that examine: <br />- The relational field <br />- Creating with this field <br />- Seeing our bodies as doorways to the field <br />- The field in relationships <br />- And much more…<br /><br />Through practical spirituality and firm underpinnings in science and personal experience, Dancing with The Field introduces a framework for life to help people recognize when they are in a state of connection and play with this field and when they are not.<br /><br />If you are on a spiritual path and feel like you need some additional guidance to bring more joy into your life, then this is the book you simply must read now!</span>

<div id="review_2831316658" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2831316658" />
    <a title="Grady" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1362506-grady"><img alt="Grady" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442472304p2/1362506.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2831316658?book_show_action=true">May 23, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Grady" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Grady" href="/user/show/1362506-grady">Grady</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2831316658" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1975182353380709113">‘Pay attention, be astonished, and tell about it’ – Mary Oliver<br/><br/>Indian born New York author Kris Kelkar experienced his first of many travels when he moved to the US, becoming a high tech entrepreneur with many inventions and patents to his credit, and built successful business based on communication skills, heart-brain coherence, the impact of relationships and thinking styles. His confrontation with health crises resulted in his marrying western medicine and complementary methods such as medita</span>
  <span id="freeText1975182353380709113" style="display:none">‘Pay attention, be astonished, and tell about it’ – Mary Oliver<br /><br />Indian born New York author Kris Kelkar experienced his first of many travels when he moved to the US, becoming a high tech entrepreneur with many inventions and patents to his credit, and built successful business based on communication skills, heart-brain coherence, the impact of relationships and thinking styles. His confrontation with health crises resulted in his marrying western medicine and complementary methods such as meditation, discovering the deep connection between mind, body and spirit. His learned techniques led to his current life as a life coach emphasizing the importance of relationships through his Third-Consciousness lessons. And this connection is the essence of this impressive book.<br /><br />In his cogent introduction Kris shares his thoughts about early life threatening experiences – ‘I have since had many experiences where it felt like I was interacting with something bigger than myself – many have been magical, mystical and ecstatic. Some involve major life threatening health crises, others involve experiences of powerful manifestations that to this day I cannot explain any other way, and some are relatively minor experiences where I see evidence of the universe conspiring to give me exactly what I want. Examples include mystically manifesting significant business opportunities that changed an industry and my fledgling company, to the emergence of life-threatening diseases where I would have died had it not been for bizarre circumstances that led to surprising diagnoses, all the way to wanting a bottle of water at a workshop and a stranger coming and handing one to me without any sense of why, or days where every traffic light magically changes in my favor right as I get to an intersection. I now see these experiences as my dancing with what I now call The Field and signs of how much in its flow and resonance I am on a given day… Though my experiences have ranged from the profoundly impactful to what I would call whimsical synchronicities, each experience has in some way transformed (or continues to transform) me – to wake me up to this greater presence in my life.’<br /><br />In this immensely accessible book Kris explains how he and his wife teach people to play the relating game so each person wins – relationships including romantic, parent-child, friendships and workplace collaborations. His thoughts are shared about the Field, influenced by both science and spirituality, that serves to connect us all in finding fullness and joy in this life. His manner of teaching is warmly compatible with the reader’s adaptation to his concepts and by the end of the book, there is a sense of enrichment and joy that provides a path to change, to play, and to emotionally and spiritually grow. Highly Recommended. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="1975182353380709113" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2813780654" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2813780654" />
    <a title="Valery" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4013735-valery"><img alt="Valery" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1480691033p2/4013735.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2813780654?book_show_action=true">May 08, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Valery" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Valery" href="/user/show/4013735-valery">Valery</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2813780654" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13713592696485710307">Dancing with the Field: Bringing Joy, Passion and Play into Everyday Life by Kris Kelkar is such a fascinating book. The field in this instance relates to the energy around us, the conscious field that surrounds us in every situation. This book examines how to acknowledge and use that field of connection to improve not only our relationships, but our lives in general. Sometimes coincidences happen in life that are inexplicable, the author reflects on a car accident that never happened when he wa</span>
  <span id="freeText13713592696485710307" style="display:none">Dancing with the Field: Bringing Joy, Passion and Play into Everyday Life by Kris Kelkar is such a fascinating book. The field in this instance relates to the energy around us, the conscious field that surrounds us in every situation. This book examines how to acknowledge and use that field of connection to improve not only our relationships, but our lives in general. Sometimes coincidences happen in life that are inexplicable, the author reflects on a car accident that never happened when he was a teen learning to drive and at a stop light. Serendipity is another way of looking at this, but it is often more, a "knowing" at a deeper level of what to do in any situation. Perhaps a field of knowing. This book is full of anecdotal evidence of a more connected way of living, the author speaks of his personal experiences in his relationships, while backing all of this up with science and a little philosophy. Wholly intriguing and enlightening, this book is highly recommended; it will open your eyes. </span>
  <a data-text-id="13713592696485710307" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2812710090" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer10958386529809855789">I think that this is one of the books that everyone should read. Kelkar presents a book that almost makes you feel like you are in the presence of a life coach, but much better as the lessons in the book are quite practical while still being underpinned on scientific concepts and practical spirituality. <br/><br/>The book is easy to read and is organized in chapters with each chapter addressing a new concept that is intertwined with other chapters to make for a wholesome guide to living a happier and more</span>
  <span id="freeText10958386529809855789" style="display:none">I think that this is one of the books that everyone should read. Kelkar presents a book that almost makes you feel like you are in the presence of a life coach, but much better as the lessons in the book are quite practical while still being underpinned on scientific concepts and practical spirituality. <br /><br />The book is easy to read and is organized in chapters with each chapter addressing a new concept that is intertwined with other chapters to make for a wholesome guide to living a happier and more fulfilling life. I like the way Kelkar explores the conscious field in an alternative way without focusing too much on religion. His style of writing is quite authentic as he mixes an accessible scientific framework with personal experiences. The book was quite eye-opening and will help everyone on a path to self-awareness.<br /></span>

<div id="review_2827515236" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2827515236" />
    <a title="Anony Mouse" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/97502457-anony-mouse"><img alt="Anony Mouse" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1558358137p2/97502457.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2827515236?book_show_action=true">May 20, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anony Mouse" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anony Mouse" href="/user/show/97502457-anony-mouse">Anony Mouse</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2827515236" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12541526307734484607">Kris Kelkar is a long-time yoga practitioner and an avid meditator who wrote this quite hard to get into book about something termed the Field and how one needs to learn how to dance with it to live a prolonged, contented life. In his own words, “he wishes to ‘share his experiences and learning so this book inspires the reader (that’s me) to explore this Field and acquire how it works and how it benefitted Kris himself.” According to him, there is magic and mystery in this Field’s paradoxical na</span>
  <span id="freeText12541526307734484607" style="display:none">Kris Kelkar is a long-time yoga practitioner and an avid meditator who wrote this quite hard to get into book about something termed the Field and how one needs to learn how to dance with it to live a prolonged, contented life. In his own words, “he wishes to ‘share his experiences and learning so this book inspires the reader (that’s me) to explore this Field and acquire how it works and how it benefitted Kris himself.” According to him, there is magic and mystery in this Field’s paradoxical nature and how it will shine for me a direction to take to live an ‘ecstatic life.’ I have to be honest with you, that throughout this book I did get a bit of its message but the downside of it was that I did not understand some concepts (scientific) that he used throughout. I realized that I will just have to read through it and hopefully note some quotes from it for this review. I know this is just me but for others it may be different.<br /><br />There was one section of this book that caught my attention though. This was what he wrote about what I deemed as telepathy that is one of the subjects I am most interested in. “Science is now validating that we each constantly transmit our thoughts and emotions through a field and this can cause resonant vibrations in those around us, resulting in the transmission of our thoughts and emotions to others. I was surprised to read this in this book because it has been an ongoing concept in my mind for so long. This notion that people can hear what others are thinking or something. I know that this book and Kelkar are specialists and are only talking from their field and therefore is not a universal truth but still.<br /><br />Other topics mentioned in this peculiar book (it is to me) are metaphysics and spirituality and religion that acts to point people to “frameworks” where (on a human-sized scale) when we make we at times “act more like matter than energy—focusing solely on worldly products and topics. I recommend this book to people who work in psychology, therapy, and meditative practices. I think this book should be read by these people only because it is laden with terms that they only can understand. I felt disappointed when I was reading this book because I am not familiar with the main topic and therefore this book was not an enjoyable experience. I hurried to complete it and thus the three stars. But on a positive note, I think this could summon a lot of experts and yoga gurus and such to lengthy educated discussions.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="12541526307734484607" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('tqed9ndNGtkDmK56K3Dr2LMGArIGE+FSsL8WF+YuU1jPqc/R5BcG4DN4nDF1gP7K6d9Sp7JMwO55RDfNEEvZYw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('nDmtUPtnbcuS7n4Nl3lJnchUqUaEpXgsi4hvFRcjNk3lN/93aD1x8qIOTEbJiVyPko35UzD6WZBCc07P4Ua8dg==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

Yet there are moments of exquisite tenderness in these troubled lives. Georgette, the transvestite who falls in love with a callous hoodlum; Tralala, the conniving prostitute who plumbs the depths of sexual degradation; and Harry, the strike leader who hides his true desires behind a boorish masculinity, are unforgettable creations. Last Exit to Brooklyn was banned by British courts in 1967, a decision that was reversed the following year with the help of a number of writers and critics including Anthony Burgess and Frank Kermode.\n\nHubert Selby, Jr. (1928-2004) was born in Brooklyn, New York. At the age of 15, he dropped out of school and went to sea with the merchant marines. While at sea he was diagnosed with lung disease. With no other way to make a living, he decided to try writing: \'I knew the alphabet. Maybe I could be a writer.\' In 1964 he completed his first book, Last Exit to Brooklyn, which has since become a cult classic. In 1966, it was the subject of an obscenity trial in the UK. His other books include The Room, The Demon, Requiem for a Dream, The Willow Tree and Waiting Period. In 2000, Requiem for a Dream was adapted into a film starring Jared Leto and Ellen Burstyn, and directed by Darren Aronofsky.\n\n\'Last Exit to Brooklyn will explode like a rusty hellish bombshell <span id="freeTextContainer6564803515142799058">Kris Kelkar has led an exciting life filled with diverse experiences. He has visited nearly 40 countries for business, pleasure and transformative healing experiences. Born in India, he came to the United States at a young age. Growing up in New York City in the early 1970s, he experienced some of the seedier sides of life. Studying engineering and business, Kris became a serial high-technology en</span>
  <span id="freeText6564803515142799058" style="display:none">Kris Kelkar has led an exciting life filled with diverse experiences. He has visited nearly 40 countries for business, pleasure and transformative healing experiences. Born in India, he came to the United States at a young age. Growing up in New York City in the early 1970s, he experienced some of the seedier sides of life. Studying engineering and business, Kris became a serial high-technology entrepreneur. Throughout his highly successful career, he created numerous inventions which were awarded over a dozen patents and helped transform industries. He also built and led successful businesses based on a foundation of non-traditional concepts such as company values, 360-relationships, thinking-styles, heart-brain coherence, and communication skills.<br /><br />Kris retired after experiencing two back-to-back life-threatening health crises which also accelerated his path of personal and spiritual growth. Addressing his cancer diagnosis through a journey of combining western medicine and complimentary approaches, he learned to heal his body, mind and spirit and also learned how they are all interconnected at a deep level. In his continuing explorations, he is passionate about how we as human beings relate to ourselves, to each other, and to the world around us - in effect embracing relationship as a spiritual path.<br /><br />A long-time yoga practitioner and an avid meditator, Kris is skilled in many meditation techniques ranging from ancient practices like Tibetan Shamatha to cutting-edge ones like Ecstatic Breathwork, Joe Dispenza, and HeartMath. He has spent over a decade engaged in intense personal transformation through many modalities spanning conscious relationship, Tantra, Orgasmic Meditation, conscious communication, energy healing and Council (a practice of deep listening derived from indigenous cultures). In each case, he dove deep and emerged with the essence of the work that he integrated into his life. Through this process, Kris earned numerous certifications to coach and teach individuals and groups using many of these modalities. <br /><br />Together with his wife Meenal, they now coach people and teach workshops that help people play the relationship game so both people win. Using their body-based framework called Third-Consciousness that incorporates lessons from their diverse training and 30 years of practice together, they continue to transform relationships and lives.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6564803515142799058" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
